================================================================================
EXECUTIVE SUMMARY — WORLD-ITEM E-PICKUP (FO4 1.11.191 next-gen)
================================================================================
(Report produced by decomp_world_pickup.py chain 1..9 + final1..4; supporting
raw scan data in appendix below this summary.)

Primary answer: the "press E on a world item -> goes to player inventory"
path lands, at the player level, on
    PlayerCharacter vtable slot[0xEC]  =  sub_140D62930   (RVA 0xD62930)

The inventory-side work (insert baseForm into player container, handle
ammo-in-weapon, clear PC.currentActivateRef, etc.) is delegated to
    sub_140500430                                          (RVA 0x500430)
which sub_140D62930 always calls internally.

The vtable slot is called via
    offset +0x760 (= 0xEC*8 = 1888) from the PlayerCharacter vptr
Only PlayerCharacter overrides slot 0xEC; TESObjectREFR::vt[0xEC] is
nullsub_5593 (i.e. it is a PC-specific virtual, not generic to REFR).

================================================================================
SIGNATURE
================================================================================
The slot 0xEC virtual has the signature:

    __int64 __fastcall
    PlayerCharacter__PickUp(
        PlayerCharacter     *this,      // rcx -- the player (qword_1432D2260)
        ObjectRefHandle     *refHandle, // rdx -- handle of world REFR being taken
        unsigned int         count,     // r8d -- # of instances (usually 1)
        char                 silent     // r9b -- 1 = suppress HUD/log messages
    );

The REFR pointer is obtained inside the body via
    sub_14027ED70(handle->rawPtr32) / sub_140436820 etc.

After REFR lookup the body of sub_140D62930 does, in order:
  1.  Handle theft/ownership arbitration (if the REFR is owned by an
      NPC): sub_140562960 / sub_140DB3DB0 / sub_140C6C2A0 path.
  2.  Rebuild ExtraContainerChanges (sub_140DABB40 loop over any
      sub-refs that belong to the worldcell containing the ref).
  3.  Call sub_140500430(player, refrPtr, count)  // <-- the real inv-add
  4.  Disable/destroy the world REFR via vt+320 (ActivateAndDisable).
  5.  Queue a "ref-taken" event (sub_140C45DC0 on queue qword_1432F46F8).
  6.  Fire "ItemsAdded" script event and play pickup sound
      (sub_141082DD0).

sub_140500430 signature:
    void __fastcall sub_140500430(_QWORD *dstActor, __int64 srcREFR,
                                  unsigned int count);
It is the actual primitive that moves the base form of srcREFR into
dstActor's inventory via sub_140502940 (the AddObject workhorse), plus
a second sub_140502940 for any ammo if the REFR base is type 43 (weapon).

================================================================================
WHO CALLS IT -> HOW DOES E-PRESS REACH vt[0xEC]?
================================================================================
Seven call sites in .text invoke `call qword ptr [reg+760h]`:

  [A]  sub_141033580 (RVA 0x1033580)
       -> MultiActivateMenu button handler.  Compares the pressed
          token against "Activate", "Accept", "Cancel", "PrevPage",
          and on "Activate"/"Accept" calls:
             qword_1432D2260->vt[0xEC](
                 qword_1432D2260,              // player
                 qword_1433074A0,              // current activate target
                                               //   REFR handle
                 1,                            // count=1
                 1                             // silent=1
             );
       **THIS IS THE USER-FACING E-PRESS PATH** -- it is the MultiActivate
       menu's "Activate" button, which the HUD invokes when the user
       presses E with a valid rollover target.

  [B]  sub_140458470 (RVA 0x458470)  -- util helper
       -> _RTDynamicCast(refr, ...Actor) then vt[0xEC](...). Called from
          35 places.  This is the generic `PickUpItem(refr, actor, cnt)`
          inline used by scripts & AI.  Specifically BGSProcedureActivate
          dispatch and some Papyrus natives (Actor.PickUpObject, etc.).

  [C]  sub_1404652F0 (RVA 0x4652F0)
       -> Steal-check wrapper.  Calls vt[0xEC] only if ownership checks
          pass; otherwise routes to sub_141033950 (steal / crime event).

  [D]  sub_140505D00 (RVA 0x505D00)
       -> ContainerMenu sub-dispatch.  Walks a1[31] (the
          ExtraContainerChanges->entries), decodes weapon/ammo extra
          data, and for *unowned* items in the opened container fires
          vt[0xEC] on the activator.  Used when the player manually
          picks something up FROM an opened container (alternate path
          besides ContainerMenu::TransferItem).

  [E]  sub_140A0A270 (RVA 0xA0A270)
       -> WorkshopMenu / build-mode: move-resource into workshop
          inventory.

  [F]  sub_140A4E690 (RVA 0xA4E690)
       -> Barter / vendor: transfer owned item to a player.

  [G]  sub_14103D3E0 (RVA 0x103D3E0)
       -> ContainerMenu withdraw mover (sub_14103E950 ==
          ContainerMenu::TransferItem, slot[21] of ContainerMenu vtable).
          Already known -- this is the withdraw side of TransferItem we
          hooked in a previous RE session.

Minimal live-picked-up flow (confirmed by decomp):
     HUD "Activate" button press
       -> input dispatcher routes to sub_141033580
       -> sub_141033580 matches *a2 == qword_14326DD10 ("Activate" token)
       -> calls qword_1432D2260->vt[0xEC](player, currentRef, 1, 1)
       -> sub_140D62930 arbitrates ownership / builds refund packet
       -> sub_140D62930 calls sub_140500430(player, ref, 1)
       -> sub_140500430 calls sub_140502940 (AddObject workhorse)
       -> sub_140502940 runs the inventory insert

================================================================================
FEEDBACK-LOOP RISK vs. vt[0x7A] (AddObjectToContainer)?
================================================================================
Call-graph BFS from sub_140D62930 at depth 6, 1705 funcs visited
(report4) found NO direct path from the pickup chain to sub_140C7A500
(= PlayerCharacter::vt[0x7A] = AddObjectToContainer).

  * sub_140500430 DOES call sub_140502940 (AddObject workhorse) directly.
  * sub_140C7A500 (vt[0x7A]) ALSO calls sub_140502940 (via a forked path
    through sub_1405007B0 which is the shared inner worker).

So:
  - vt[0x7A] handler (AddObjectToContainer) never fires during a
    world pickup.  Confirmed: the live log said so, BFS confirms no
    indirect reach either.
  - Conversely, sub_140D62930 / sub_140500430 are NOT reached by
    vt[0x7A] / container-menu transfer flows (no shared convergence
    upstream of the workhorse).
  - The two paths meet ONLY at the workhorse sub_140502940, which is
    the universal final insert and should NOT be hooked.

Therefore hooking vt[0x7A] AND vt[0xEC] in parallel causes NO
double-fire, NO feedback loop. They capture orthogonal transfer
categories:
  - vt[0x7A]  : container<->player (chest, corpse, ContainerMenu TAKE).
  - vt[0xEC]  : world-item pickup (stimpak on table, ammo on floor,
                weapon leaning on a wall, holodisk, etc.) AND
                ContainerMenu withdraw (via sub_14103D3E0), AND
                barter/workshop moves, AND Actor.PickUpObject script
                calls.

Net: **vt[0xEC] is a SUPERSET of "world pickup" -- it also catches
ContainerMenu withdraw and barter**.  If you only want world-pickup
and not to duplicate ContainerMenu-withdraw packets already sent by
the vt[0x7A] hook, you need an in-handler filter.

================================================================================
BEST HOOK STRATEGY
================================================================================

Option 1 (RECOMMENDED): MinHook on sub_140D62930 directly.
  - RVA 0xD62930 is stable for 1.11.191 next-gen.
  - Only 1 .rdata placement (PlayerCharacter vtable slot 0xEC).  No
    inlining risk because all 7 call sites dispatch via virtual
    through vt[0xEC].
  - Trampoline signature:
        char WINAPI Hooked_PlayerCharacter__PickUp(
            PlayerCharacter *this,
            ObjectRefHandle *refHandle,
            unsigned int     count,
            char             silent);
  - At entry: deref refHandle to REFR*, read +0xE0 to get baseForm,
    read +0x14 of baseForm for BASE formID, read +0x14 of ref for
    REF formID, then send packet.

Option 2: Patch PC vtable slot[0xEC] at RVA 0x2564838 + 0xEC*8 = 0x2564F98.
  - Slightly lower-level (survives MinHook incompatibilities).  But
    MinHook on the function itself is simpler and equivalent.

Option 3: Hook the caller sub_141033580 (MultiActivateMenu "Activate"
button).  **Not recommended** -- this misses:
    - Barter / workshop transfer inputs,
    - Papyrus Actor.PickUpObject script calls,
    - AI-driven pickups (BGSProcedureActivate).
  If you truly want ONLY "user pressed E in world", this is the
  sharpest filter but loses script-driven pickups (which you
  probably DO want to sync for multiplayer).

================================================================================
DISTINGUISHING WORLD-PICKUP FROM OTHER TRANSFERS INSIDE THE HOOK
================================================================================

Inside sub_140D62930 ("PickUp") there is NO simple flag that says
"this came from world vs container".  What you CAN use to filter:

  (a) Look at *refHandle -> ref* and read ref->parentCell (+0xB8).
      If parentCell is set and worldspace is non-null  -> **world pickup**.
      If parentCell is null or the ref's enclosing container is not
      a worldcell  -> container-menu withdraw or barter.

  (b) Check the thread-local guard set by the vt[0x7A] hook (it is
      SET for ContainerMenu TransferItem and for corpse loot).  If
      the guard is clear during vt[0xEC] entry, you are almost
      certainly on the world-pickup or workshop path.

  (c) The current rollover REFR is stored at qword_1433074A0 (set by
      sub_141033580 before the call).  If refHandle->ref ==
      qword_1433074A0 at hook entry, user pressed E on the crosshair
      target.  Otherwise it is a script or menu dispatch.

  (d) Inside sub_140500430 check *(qword_1432D2260 + 3368) == srcREFR.
      Player offset +0xD28 = "CurrentActivateRef" -- this is the
      crosshair item.  If equal, it's the world pickup the user
      triggered.

Recommended filter for "ghost player world pickup packet only":
      (user_activate_ref_is_crosshair)
         AND (parentCell_is_worldspace || parentCell_is_interior_cell)
         AND (!vt7a_guard_active)
      -> send_pickup_packet(player, baseFormId, cellId, count)

  sub_140C4CE00       RVA 0xC4CE00   -- main-thread event pump
                                       (case 133 -> sub_140CA7D20)

  sub_140436820                      -- REFR name/debug builder
  qword_1432D2260     RVA 0x32D2260  -- PlayerCharacter singleton
  qword_1433074A0                    -- current rollover REFR handle
                                       (what the crosshair targets)
  PlayerCharacter +0xD28 (3368)      -- CurrentActivateRef pointer
                                       (set by activation, cleared at
                                        end of sub_140500430)
  PlayerCharacter vtable             RVA 0x2564838
  PlayerCharacter vt[0xEC]           offset +0x760 from vptr
  TESObjectREFR vtable               RVA 0x249CBC8  (DIFFERENT from
                                       the runtime vtable at
                                       0x2564838 which is the
                                       PlayerCharacter vtable.  This
                                       contradicts the previous
                                       reference_fo4_offsets.md line
                                       that said 0x2564838 is the
                                       "TESObjectREFR vtable" -- it
                                       is actually the PlayerCharacter
                                       vtable.  But because PC inherits
                                       TESObjectREFR the slot numbers
                                       for REFR-defined virtuals
                                       match up.)
